  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d2c93d15-0dd4-45cd-a76e-6c4850f51e09'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer2091958585860405959">In print since 1948, this is a single-volume collection of Oscar Wilde's texts. It contains his only novel, The Portrait of Dorian Gray as well as his plays, stories, poems, essays and letters. Illustrated with many photographs, the book includes introductions to each section by Wilde's grandon, Merlin Holoand, Owen Dudley Edwards, Declan Kibertd and Terence Brown. A compr</span>
  <span id="freeText2091958585860405959" style="display:none">In print since 1948, this is a single-volume collection of Oscar Wilde's texts. It contains his only novel, The Portrait of Dorian Gray as well as his plays, stories, poems, essays and letters. Illustrated with many photographs, the book includes introductions to each section by Wilde's grandon, Merlin Holoand, Owen Dudley Edwards, Declan Kibertd and Terence Brown. A comprehensive bibliography of works by and about Oscar Wilde together with a chronological table of his life and work are also included.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1551731321" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1746687175387742524"><b>HAPPY BIRTHDAY, SON! YOU DID WELL! ♥</b><br/><br/>Almost three years and 1,270 pages later I'm finally marking this as read, what a surreal feeling. I cannot believe that I have read every single word of Oscar's published writing. I know, they're are still many private letters left for me to discover but, you guys, <b>I did it.</b> I am proud of myself and I am proud of my trash son. I don't think I'll ever love an author as much as I love Oscar. <br/><br/>Here's to the man who believed when he died that his name would be tox</span>
  <span id="freeText1746687175387742524" style="display:none"><b>HAPPY BIRTHDAY, SON! YOU DID WELL! ♥</b><br /><br />Almost three years and 1,270 pages later I'm finally marking this as read, what a surreal feeling. I cannot believe that I have read every single word of Oscar's published writing. I know, they're are still many private letters left for me to discover but, you guys, <b>I did it.</b> I am proud of myself and I am proud of my trash son. I don't think I'll ever love an author as much as I love Oscar. <br /><br />Here's to the man who believed when he died that his name would be toxic for generations to come. For hundreds of years his works wouldn't be read. He would stand for nothing but perversion; utter disgust of a society that couldn't bear people like him. Oh, how wrong you were, my darling child. You're still one of the most read authors in the 21th century and we all love and appreciate you very much. They even had to lock up your sarcophagus because people wouldn't stop kissing it. I wish I could wake you up for five minutes to tell you that, then you could go back to sleep again. &lt;3<br /><br />And because I am a good hoe and gracious queen I will leave you with all of my <span id="freeTextContainer17370085448141295194">Wilde has such a gift with phrasing, I always think about how parallel he seems to me with Ryan Adams. So many accolades so early, then such a fever to tear him apart.<br/><br/>Here's a few quotes:<br/><br/>A little sincerity is a dangerous thing, and a great deal of it is absolutely fatal.<br/><br/>A man can be happy with any woman as long as he does not love her.<br/> <br/>Always forgive your enemies; nothing annoys them so much. <br/><br/>America is the only country that went from barbarism to decadence without civilization in between. <br/><br/>Anyon</span>
  <span id="freeText17370085448141295194" style="display:none">Wilde has such a gift with phrasing, I always think about how parallel he seems to me with Ryan Adams. So many accolades so early, then such a fever to tear him apart.<br /><br />Here's a few quotes:<br /><br />A little sincerity is a dangerous thing, and a great deal of it is absolutely fatal.<br /><br />A man can be happy with any woman as long as he does not love her.<br /> <br />Always forgive your enemies; nothing annoys them so much. <br /><br />America is the only country that went from barbarism to decadence without civilization in between. <br /><br />Anyone who lives within their means suffers from a lack of imagination.<br /><br />Arguments are to be avoided; they are always vulgar and often convincing.<br /><br />Biography lends to death a new terror.<br /> <br />Consistency is the last refuge of the unimaginative.<br /> <br />Every portrait that is painted with feeling is a portrait of the artist, not of the sitter.<br /><br />Fashion is a form of ugliness so intolerable that we have to alter it every six months.<br /><br />Genius is born--not paid.<br /><br />I always like to know everything about my new friends, and nothing about my old ones.<br /><br />I am not young enough to know everything.<br /><br />I think that God in creating Man somewhat overestimated his ability.<br /><br />If you want to tell people the truth, make them laugh, otherwise they'll kill you.<br /><br />Illusion is the first of all pleasures.<br /><br />It is always a silly thing to give advice, but to give good advice is fatal.<br /><br />Man is least himself when he talks in his own person. Give him a mask, and he will tell you the truth.<br /><br />Morality, like art, means drawing a line someplace.<br /><br />Most people are other people. Their thoughts are someone elses opinions, their lives a mimicry, their passions a quotation.<br /><br />One can survive everything, nowadays, except death, and live down everything except a good reputation.<br /><br />One should always play fairly when one has the winning cards.<br /><br />Patriotism is the virtue of the vicious.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15544368494763849997">So essential it's not even funny. Not a better writer in the English language. Also if one can have a hero in this world, I think Wilde can fit that bill. He maybe the first writer that I realize was a rebel of sorts. My first actual rock n' roll figure that I looked up to.<br/><br/>I started reading Wilde as a young teenager - due to the fact that he seemed to be the most glamourous figure in literature. Most of my high school friends were into the Beats or such toss as Jonathan Bach, but Wilde was my (a</span>
  <span id="freeText15544368494763849997" style="display:none">So essential it's not even funny. Not a better writer in the English language. Also if one can have a hero in this world, I think Wilde can fit that bill. He maybe the first writer that I realize was a rebel of sorts. My first actual rock n' roll figure that I looked up to.<br /><br />I started reading Wilde as a young teenager - due to the fact that he seemed to be the most glamourous figure in literature. Most of my high school friends were into the Beats or such toss as Jonathan Bach, but Wilde was my (as T-Rex's Marc Bolan would say ) mainman. And the fact that I am straight to be attracted to such a guy figure had a great importance in my life. Wilde represented a third way to me. The fact that he was outside of his culture appealed to my aesthetic - plus it was sexy.<br /><br />Oscar Wilde, born in the 19th Century and dying in the new 20th Century - was truly an artist of the 20th Century. Oscar Wilde I salute you!</span>

<div id="review_3156362351" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3156362351" />
    <a title="DJ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41664104-dj"><img alt="DJ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578657426p2/41664104.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3156362351?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="DJ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="DJ" href="/user/show/41664104-dj">DJ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11410585-complete-works-of-oscar-wilde">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41664104-dj?shelf=collections">collections</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41664104-dj?shelf=published-1800s">published-1800s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41664104-dj?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41664104-dj?shelf=male-author">male-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41664104-dj?shelf=lgbtqia">lgbtqia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41664104-dj?shelf=britain-ireland">britain-ireland</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3156362351" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17719437615361691890">Before starting this collection I had actually never read anything by Oscar Wilde - I have now read <i>everything</i> by Oscar Wilde, and can officially say I am a massive fan! His writing is incredibly clever and witty, but also riveting, humorous and beautiful. My favourites would be <i>The Importance of Being Earnest, The Picture of Dorian Gray, The Happy Prince & Other Tales, The Ballad of Reading Gaol,</i> and <i>De Profundis</i>. <br/><br/>The works included - and my general opinion of them - are as follows: <br/><br/><b>
  <u>PLAYS:</u>
</b><br/>V</span>
  <span id="freeText17719437615361691890" style="display:none">Before starting this collection I had actually never read anything by Oscar Wilde - I have now read <i>everything</i> by Oscar Wilde, and can officially say I am a massive fan! His writing is incredibly clever and witty, but also riveting, humorous and beautiful. My favourites would be <i>The Importance of Being Earnest, The Picture of Dorian Gray, The Happy Prince &amp; Other Tales, The Ballad of Reading Gaol,</i> and <i>De Profundis</i>. <br /><br />The works included - and my general opinion of them - are as follows: <br /><br /><b>
  <u>PLAYS:</u>
</b><br />Vera, or The Nihilists - 3 Stars ⭐️⭐️⭐️<br />The Duchess of Padua - 2 Stars ⭐️⭐️<br />Lady Windermere’s Fan - 5 Stars ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br />A Woman of No Importance - 5 Stars ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br />An Ideal Husband - 4 Stars ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br />The Importance of Being Earnest - 5 Stars ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br />Salomé - 3 Stars ⭐️⭐️⭐️<br />La Saint Courtisane - 3 Stars ⭐️⭐️⭐️<br />A Florentine Tragedy - 4 Stars ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br /><br /><b>
  <u>NOVEL:</u>
</b><br />The Picture of Dorian Gray - 5 Stars ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br /><br /><b>
  <u>STORIES &amp; FAIRY-TALES:</u>
</b><br />The Happy Prince and Other Tales - 5 Stars ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br /> <i>- The Happy Prince - 5 Stars</i><br /> <i>- The Nightingale and the Rose - 5 Stars</i> <br /> <i>- The Selfish Giant - 4 Stars</i> <br /> <i>- The Devoted Friend - 5 Stars</i> <br /> <i>- The Remarkable Rocket - 5 Stars</i> <br />Lord Arthur Saville’s Crime and Other Stories - 4 Stars ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br /> <i>- Lord Arthur Saville’s Crime - 4 Stars</i> <br /> <i>- The Canterville Ghost - 5 Stars</i> <br /> <i>- The Sphinx Without a Secret - 4 Stars</i> <br /> <i>- The Model Millionaire- 4 Stars</i> <br /> <i>- The Portrait of Mr W.H. - 1.5 Stars</i> <br />A House of Pomegranates - 2 Stars ⭐️⭐️<br /> <i>- The Young King - 2 Stars <br /> - The Birthday of the Infanta - 2 Stars <br /> - The Fisherman and His Soul - 3 Stars <br /> - The Star-Child - 3 Stars</i> <br /><br /><b>
  <u>POEMS:</u>
</b><br />The Complete Poems - 4 Stars ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br />The Ballad of Reading Gaol (special mention) - 5 Stars ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br /><br /><b>
  <u>ESSAYS AND LETTERS:</u>
</b><br />De Profundis - 5 Stars ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br />And in the spirit of complete honesty, I actually didn’t read the other essays included in the collection - <i>Intentions</i> and <i>The Soul of Man Under Socialism</i> - as I knew they wouldn’t interest me, and so they have not affected my rating.</span>

<div id="review_780675188" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/780675188" />
    <a title="Aurélien Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19341029-aur-lien-thomas"><img alt="Aurélien Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568508113p2/19341029.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/780675188?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aurélien Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aurélien Thomas" href="/user/show/19341029-aur-lien-thomas">Aurélien Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007144365" href="/book/show/864217.Complete_Works_of_Oscar_Wilde">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19341029-aur-lien-thomas?shelf=british-literature">british-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19341029-aur-lien-thomas?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer780675188" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15900493945223410455">I remember discovering Oscar Wilde with 'The Picture of Dorian Gray', a luscious and decadent read which, ironically enough, had not only made his success but also caused his downfall (being quoted ad nauseam during his trial). Well, Oscar Wilde, we know, finally ended up in jail. His work from behind bars is, about, really touching. <br/><br/>First, <i>'De Profundis'</i>, his letter to his lover, is an insightful take upon his fate - the pain of a man looked upon, ruined and humiliated, who nevertheless has the</span>
  <span id="freeText15900493945223410455" style="display:none">I remember discovering Oscar Wilde with 'The Picture of Dorian Gray', a luscious and decadent read which, ironically enough, had not only made his success but also caused his downfall (being quoted ad nauseam during his trial). Well, Oscar Wilde, we know, finally ended up in jail. His work from behind bars is, about, really touching. <br /><br />First, <i>'De Profundis'</i>, his letter to his lover, is an insightful take upon his fate - the pain of a man looked upon, ruined and humiliated, who nevertheless has the unforgiving lucidity to don't spare himself for his mistakes. For sure, it reeks of a sad bitterness. It is, nevertheless, so honest it's quite disarming. Then, his <i>'The Ballad of Reading Gaol'</i>. Powerful verses, grim but deeply heartfelt, here's one of his most intense text, and surely one of his best work. Well, as far as I am concerned, it certainly stands out from the rest of his poetry!<br /><br />His <i>'Poems'</i> indeed are, overall, quite bad. A classicist at heart, Oscar Wilde attempted to follow strict formal rules that are everything but suited to his stylised and flowery language, going over the top and feeling way too rigid. I preferred his <i>'Prose Poems'</i>, where he tossed off such strictness to completely unleash himself. In fact, mostly religious (mystic?) his prose displays him at his playful-best. <br /><br />As for the plays... I am not one for theatre; it's just not my cup of tea. I have to say though that I absolutely enjoyed reading most of his! <i>'Lady Windermere's Fan'</i> (my personal favourite), <i>'The Importance of Being Earnest'</i>, <i>'A Woman of No Importance'</i>… Oscar Wilde is witty, sharp, cynical and sarcastic, always catching the reader off-guard with the unexpected, and his creativity and bluntness are a delight that takes no prisoner. I just struggled with <i>'An Ideal Husband'</i>, predictable, too long, and tiring for its feel of déja vu. I didn't know he had written a tragedy (<i>'The Duchess of Padua'</i>), which was a nice surprise, especially since it's a really good play overall. My favourite remains, however, <i>'Salomé'</i> - wonderfully poetic, dark, occult, bathed in bloody moonlight, all here is but foggy vision dancing enthrallingly before our hypnotised eyes. <br /><br />Noteworthy too are his essays on Art. <i>'Intentions'</i> and <i>'The Decay of Lying'</i> may not be ground breaking, but they deserve a read to better understand what he meant by some of his most famous (and misunderstood!) quotes -e.g. 'life imitates art' and the like... His tales are entertaining too, though I disliked the ones he wrote for children (all unsuited and complete failure).<br /><br />All in all then, here's a great compilation. It can feel unequal (again, some of his work was really bad -most of his poems, a few tales...) but, considering how far ranging, creative, sharp and, above all, so unique such a writer was, it's impossible to don't be in awe. A pure jewel, that deserves to adorn the personal libraries of every lovers of literature..</span>
  <a data-text-id="15900493945223410455" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_360676475" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/360676475" />
    <a title="El" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/83144-el"><img alt="El" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1479156984p2/83144.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/360676475?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="El" class="user" itemprop="url" name="El" href="/user/show/83144-el">El</a>
      </span>

          marked it as to-read




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83144-el?shelf=pause-button">pause-button</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer360676475" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10325663707317946779">This review is a work-in-progress. My review is behind that link; knock yourself out.<br/><br/>Individual reviews will be linked here as I go along, just to really annoy everyone each time it pops up in their updates</span>

<div id="review_1250304632" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1250304632" />
    <a title="Shawn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1697111-shawn"><img alt="Shawn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588366811p2/1697111.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1250304632?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shawn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shawn" href="/user/show/1697111-shawn">Shawn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1697111-shawn?shelf=r-comp-fant-19th-dno">r-comp-fant-19th-dno</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1250304632" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8356960359481008861">Okay, as recently, I'm mopping up some titles from "To Read Short Fiction Lists", genre and lit, and as I'm in the W's....<br/><br/>I had 3 pieces from Wilde on the list - I've previously read a *bit* of him (about 10 stories, mostly thanks to Dedalus Books Decadence series) but, for example, haven't tackled an obvious must-read like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12346651.The_Picture_of_Dorian_Grey' title='The Picture of Dorian Grey by Oscar Wilde' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Picture of Dorian Grey</a>.<br/><br/>"Lord Arthur Savile's Crime" is probably the most "Wildean" thing here, and in it one can see Wilde's black humor and some origins of a writer like</span>
  <span id="freeText8356960359481008861" style="display:none">Okay, as recently, I'm mopping up some titles from "To Read Short Fiction Lists", genre and lit, and as I'm in the W's....<br /><br />I had 3 pieces from Wilde on the list - I've previously read a *bit* of him (about 10 stories, mostly thanks to Dedalus Books Decadence series) but, for example, haven't tackled an obvious must-read like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12346651.The_Picture_of_Dorian_Grey" title="The Picture of Dorian Grey by Oscar Wilde" rel="nofollow noopener">The Picture of Dorian Grey</a>.<br /><br />"Lord Arthur Savile's Crime" is probably the most "Wildean" thing here, and in it one can see Wilde's black humor and some origins of a writer like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6076026.Saki" title="Saki" rel="nofollow noopener">Saki</a> (in one direction) and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7963.P_G__Wodehouse" title="P.G. Wodehouse" rel="nofollow noopener">P.G. Wodehouse</a> (in another). British upper crust life had advanced to such a point, seemingly, that one could be terribly naughty by writing a deliberately lighthearted piece about cold-blooded attempted murder, poison and anarchist bombs. Shocking! That may sound like I'm being sarcastic but actually I'm not, it's just interesting to me how levels of privilege, culture, comfort and stability (timed historically differently, of course, across varied social and class strata) invariably give rise to an impulse like this, a turning inward, a jaundiced view of the status quo, satirically and cheekily expressed. So here we have a society party of humorous cartoons (lots of witty bon mots tossed around - "The world is a stage but the play is poorly cast.") where a nobleman (Lord Savile, natch) has his palm read and is told he will commit murder in the future. Being a good upstanding chap, and not wanting to ruin his intended nuptials, he sets about trying to figure out who the least important person is that he can murder in his social circle. Hilarity ensues as poison, bombs and drownings prove ineffective until chance steps in. Of course, part of the joke is that Savile never questions (and we should never expect him to question) the accuracy of such a prediction from a dubious source, because then the ultimate joke of basing your actions on dubious sources, and the empty trendiness of the moneyed classes (and possibly their coldness to human suffering) would be undone.<br /><br />"The Star Child" is Wilde operating in his Fairy Tale Mode. In many ways it is a traditional fairy tale with an obvious moral - a poor family finds an abandoned baby and raises him to be a beautiful boy. But the boy is cruel, arrogant and hateful and despises the poverty around him, torturing small animals and displaying his ingratitude at every opportunity, so magically he is turned ugly and has to go forth in the world to learn humility - which he does, by trying to complete three impossible tasks, aided by animal servitors. The Wildean punch, when it comes, lies not so much in the classically-beautiful-but-cruel main character but instead in the short and oddly ominous last line of the piece, as if Wilde could not completely commit himself to the eternal awe and wonder of happily ever after.<br /><br />"The Decay Of Lying" is an essay (presented as a dialogue) and, honestly, I'll probably need to give it another read and dissect it at my leisure at a later date because I was mostly in the wrong head-space when I read it. Essentially, it's Wilde's barbed answer to the rise of the Naturalist/Realist movement in literature (Zola, etc.), which eschewed imagination and flights of fancy for close observations of the real world and people. Wilde believes this idea is terrible and sketches out what he believes literature (and almost almost all art) should consist of, how it should proceed and what its goals should be. Sui generis, inventive and imaginative, essentially - "effective lying" is the ultimate creativity.<br /><br />Having recently codified my own approach to the arts (well, certainly literature) as that of a Generalist/Surveyor, I can't take an us/them, good/bad argument about literature *so* seriously. I find such screeds fascinating - not as an expression of "the truth" but as "one way of looking at things" (from a particular position, in a particular moment in time, given what has come before, what was happening then and what was to come) - even as my mind begins to undermine the argument (and, in case I haven't made my point, I'd have the same reaction to a po-faced essay about the obvious superiority of realism over imagination). These kind of essays/arguments *are* important - it *was* important that someone had them and they *remain* important as records of thought processes, as we try to move forward - except we don't seem to be moving forward very much and those records seem to be ignored, as we seem to JUST KEEP HAVING the same binary us/them, good/bad stupid/reductive arguments over and over again even centuries later (just recently, in my life in fact).<br /><br />I do believe the human mind is vast and can hold many ideas, some of them contradictory. I do not think there is only one way to "do art" or that the term "art" is pretentious, or that "entertainment" is below contempt for that matter, OR that a perfect blending of "art" and "entertainment" is the Ultimate Goal for THAT matter. I do think that different approaches yield different results and have different successes, achievements, failures and traps. This doesn't seem very hard for me at all and I wonder why people seem so driven into singular conceptions - perhaps it's the varied arrogance and insecurity underlying the desperately clung-to worldviews? So, for example, when I read this essay I find it fascinating: Wilde is witty (duh), charming, intelligent and erudite and his argument makes sense - until I remember that some realist novels have, in my life, packed just as much impact as the imaginative ones. I look at what he's saying and think "hmmm, interesting that the Decadents take *part* of his stance - invention and artificiality - and discard others - by focusing on the dregs and degradation of real life". I think of genre writers who bristle at being labelled escapist and regularly chalk up straight Lit as "boring" - thus placing them in Wilde's camp - yet Wilde would be appalled to find them worrying over research, realistic detail and promoting social causes and the underrepresented.<br /><br />But I'll have to reread it. There's a good argument to be made that Wilde is deliberately overstating his case so as to have a kind of unspoken criticisms of its excesses built right into the text. Still, lots of fun!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8356960359481008861" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I remember feeling a little doubtful for buying such an expensive book from an author I had never </span>
  <span id="freeText2450604486845752581" style="display:none">A must-have for every lover of literature. Oscar Wilde is a writer like no other. His words speak directly to one's heart, their soul, their subconsciousness.. He changed the way I understood writing and reading entirely, made me fall in love with his every word and get lost in his ideas, his thoughts, his world.<br /><br />I was 13 or 14 when I first picked up a paperback copy of his complete works on a whim. I remember feeling a little doubtful for buying such an expensive book from an author I had never heard of before. Needless to say, I'm so glad I did. It's a book to read, adore, and re-read a thousand times.</span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer46617758" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7264604961381240299">I love Oscar Wilde. His tales have been part of my life since I was a child. In my teenager years his plays were the "shelter" when I felt sad. His work is wonderful, but, in this special edition, you can find everything he wrote, even the poems (which are not so good as his other works to me). I have a 1968 edition of this Collins Classics with beautiful illustrations and a great introduction by Vyvyan Holland. Beautiful edition!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

      </span>

        rated it

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/97068731-ella?shelf=oscar-wilde-aestheticism-etc">oscar-wilde-aestheticism-etc</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3280839508" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11236042097512567021">Last summer, I bought this 1,114 page book from a used bookstore in Gallway, Ireland for €6 (what a steal!). It was the second Oscar Wilde book I had bought that trip (along with an Oscar Wilde tea towel and calendar). Packing light is stupid anyways.<br/><br/>And, of course, now, during quarantine, is the perfect time to read it.<br/><br/>I wonder what Oscar Wilde would be doing during the pandemic. Okay I digress.<br/><br/>Now that I’m done it feels surreal (1,000 amazing oh my god). But this book was great because I had h</span>
  <span id="freeText11236042097512567021" style="display:none">Last summer, I bought this 1,114 page book from a used bookstore in Gallway, Ireland for €6 (what a steal!). It was the second Oscar Wilde book I had bought that trip (along with an Oscar Wilde tea towel and calendar). Packing light is stupid anyways.<br /><br />And, of course, now, during quarantine, is the perfect time to read it.<br /><br />I wonder what Oscar Wilde would be doing during the pandemic. Okay I digress.<br /><br />Now that I’m done it feels surreal (1,000 amazing oh my god). But this book was great because I had had no idea about some of his shorter stories and poems and plays and found new favorites! <br /><br />Here is a list of Oscar’s best, most well-known works:<br />- The Picture of Dorian Gray <br />- The Importance of Being Earnest<br />- Lady Windermere’s Fan<br />- A Woman of No Importance<br />- An Idea Husband<br />- The Ballad of Reading Goal<br />- De Profundis<br /><br />Here’s a list of other works that I really liked:<br />- The Canterville Ghost<br />- Lord Arthur Savile’s Crime<br />- The Duchess of Padua<br />- The Happy Prince<br />- The poems Requiescat, At Verona, and Silentium Amoris <br />- The Portrait of Mr. W. H. <br /><br />I’d highly recommend Oscar Wilde. I’m not even going to try to explain how much and why I love his work because as neither Critic nor Artist, I cannot do it justice. <br /><br />Anyways, thank you Oscar, for all of the 1,114 pages of published writing I’ve read in the past 5 weeks. I loved it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11236042097512567021" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17194696787929243606">I actually hate having all my Wilde in one volume. But now I've got this great big book which refuses to be curled up with -- I should never have sold my individual <em>Earnest</em>. Still, it's nice to have access to Wilde-ian works I probably wouldn't own otherwise.</span>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3205983-se-panoply?shelf=lgbt-literature">lgbt-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3205983-se-panoply?shelf=autobiographical">autobiographical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3205983-se-panoply?shelf=plays">plays</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer86787476" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15418583659112426794"><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://bookwayfarer.wordpress.com/2013/06/21/complete-works-of-oscar-wilde/'>http://bookwayfarer.wordpress.com/201...</a><br/>When I first read this I wasn't necessarily a fan of Oscar Wilde. I was just curious about his work and I realized the easiest and fastest way to read it all was just to buy the book and call it a day.<br/><br/>Overall a very interesting and relatively quick read. Interesting in the sense of getting everything. Background history, the fairy tales, plays, novel, essays are all accounted for, and quick to read in the fact of most everything in this book can be breezed</span>
  <span id="freeText15418583659112426794" style="display:none"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://bookwayfarer.wordpress.com/2013/06/21/complete-works-of-oscar-wilde/">http://bookwayfarer.wordpress.com/201...</a><br />When I first read this I wasn't necessarily a fan of Oscar Wilde. I was just curious about his work and I realized the easiest and fastest way to read it all was just to buy the book and call it a day.<br /><br />Overall a very interesting and relatively quick read. Interesting in the sense of getting everything. Background history, the fairy tales, plays, novel, essays are all accounted for, and quick to read in the fact of most everything in this book can be breezed through with no real issue.<br /><br />The only problem for me was near the end of the book. The poems and the essays seemed to drag on and on. One reason is, I'm not really a poetry reader usually, so it was a little painful since it was poetry and I wasn't about to skip it since, it's my book and I don't like wasting money if I'm not going to read the whole thing. Secondly, most of the essay's seemed repetitious and some were just longer than necessary. I realize everything Oscar Wilde ever wrote is included, but this is what I've learned and care to share. The only one of the essays that I didn't really mind reading was De Profundis. It was genuinely interesting since it was about the man who put him in prison and was written to him from prison.<br /><br />Otherwise I have no regrets in buying this book. It was definitely worth the $10 I put into it and I would definitely recommend this to anyone who is interested in reading the whole kaboodle of Wilde's work.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer42119649" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12786589832848808044">Oscar Wilde is always so delightful, although what disturbing children's stories! I certainly would never read those stories to a child, with the exception of 'The Remarkable Rocket'. My favorite short stories were 'Lord Arthur Savile's Crime' and 'The Canterville Ghost'. <br/> <br/>Reading all the plays back to back does cause them to blend together just a bit, he had a habit of reusing his favorite lines over and over again. Overall I would say I enjoyed 'Vera' (The Nihilists) the most, which was the on</span>
  <span id="freeText12786589832848808044" style="display:none">Oscar Wilde is always so delightful, although what disturbing children's stories! I certainly would never read those stories to a child, with the exception of 'The Remarkable Rocket'. My favorite short stories were 'Lord Arthur Savile's Crime' and 'The Canterville Ghost'. <br /> <br />Reading all the plays back to back does cause them to blend together just a bit, he had a habit of reusing his favorite lines over and over again. Overall I would say I enjoyed 'Vera' (The Nihilists) the most, which was the only play I had never heard of before purchasing this book. I wonder if 'De Profundis' should really be included, it is an interesting glimpse into his personal life but I could have done without his rambling religious views and much too long rehashing of everything that ever went wrong in his relationship. </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1153085?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="angie haney" class="user" itemprop="url" name="angie haney" href="/user/show/82459-angie-haney">angie haney</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">By all means YES!</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1153085" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8983131382743992445">This is THE book. Oscar Wilde writes with so much heart. His stories just ooze heart. Of all of his writings, Dorian Grey is probably my least favorite, and it is a masterpiece! The Happy Prince will tear your heart out. It is the most beautiful story I have ever read in my entire life. It is one of the things in my life that touched my heart so deeply that all I could do was cry at it's raw, pure, beauty. Every story has that same pure loveliness. This is a book that you can read over and over </span>
  <span id="freeText8983131382743992445" style="display:none">This is THE book. Oscar Wilde writes with so much heart. His stories just ooze heart. Of all of his writings, Dorian Grey is probably my least favorite, and it is a masterpiece! The Happy Prince will tear your heart out. It is the most beautiful story I have ever read in my entire life. It is one of the things in my life that touched my heart so deeply that all I could do was cry at it's raw, pure, beauty. Every story has that same pure loveliness. This is a book that you can read over and over and everytime it still just melts your heart. I am so in love with this book! Oh, to have been a gay man in Oscar Wilde's time! I would have been the Adam to his Steve any day! </span>
  <a data-text-id="8983131382743992445" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer626363833" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10570859213438832565">I love his fairy tales and stories. I love Dorian Gray, and I love his playfulness when it comes to questions of morality. <br/>It was therefore so sad to read his 'De Profundis'. Although written under extreme conditions, and therefore miraculously coherent, it revealed such a bitterness and moral disapproval on the part of the author. Did it diminish the magnitude of his genius? I'm not sure...</span>

          </span>
        </div>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer4304757" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9211469459393827521">Wilde should be read by everyone looking for a mixture of wit, humor and deep emotion. While some of his works are less accessible than others (I prefer his plays to his poetry) there's something in here for everyone.<br/><br/>I read his fables when I was about 7, and still recall them vividly.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('JjYZMQNU4Sijgy2f6XNLKaaER76KR1NUH8UL3VbCQb9elvgUU/k5iJhjXYRobPKV0A+09hjLSY6Lb97+lD2WTw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('khoK/PEAWFFFLDCqLUA1rlI5+n119W9zyVi3D+LSlDzquuvZoa2A8X7MQLGsX4wSJLIJNed5dald8mIsIC1DzA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

His tales and poems brim with psychological depth, almost painful intensity, and unexpected—and surprisingly modern—flashes of dark humor and irony.\n\nThis anthology offers an exceptionally generous selection of Poe\'s short stories. It includes his famed masterpieces, such as &quot;The Murders in the Rue Morgue&quot; and &quot;The Purloined Letter,&quot; featuring Poe\'s great detective, Dupin; his insightful studies of madness &quot;The Black Cat&quot; and &quot;The Tell-Tale Heart&quot;; &quot;The Gold-Bug,&quot; his delightful exercise in &quot;code-breaking&quot;; and important but lesser-known tales, such as &quot;Bon-Bon,&quot; &quot;The Assignation,&quot; and &quot;King Pest.&quot; Also included are some of Poe\'s most beloved poems, haunting lyrics of love and loss, such as &quot;Annabel Lee,&quot; nightmare phantasmagories such as &quot;The Raven,&quot; and his grand experiment in translating sound into words, &quot;The Bells.&quot;\n\nBenjamin F. Fisher, Professor of English, University of Mississippi, is a longtime enthusiast of the works of Poe. He has published books, articles, and notes about Poe, and in American, Victorian, and Gothic studies, and serves on editorial boards for several professional journals. The first playwright to depict suffering without reference to the gods, Euripides made his characters speak in human terms and face the consequences of their actions. In Medea, a woman rejected by her lover takes hideous revenge by murdering the children they both love, and Hecabe depicts the former queen of Troy, driven mad by the prospect of her daughter’s sacrifice to Achilles. Electra portrays a young woman planning to avenge the brutal death of her father at the hands of her mother, while in Heracles the hero seeks vengeance against the evil king who has caused bloodshed in his family. Philip Vellacott’s lucid translation is accompanied by an introduction, which discusses the literary background of Classical Athens and examines the distinction between instinctive and civilized Here, brought together in one volume for the first time, in a masterly new translation by the award-winning translator<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText9469096361487491367\" style=\"display:none\">Anton Chekhov, widely hailed as the supreme master of the short story, also wrote five works long enough to be called short novels. Here, brought together in one volume for the first time, in a masterly new translation by the award-winning translators Richard Pevear and Larissa Volokhonsky.The Steppe—the most lyrical of the five—is an account of a nine-year-old boy’s frightening journey by wagon train across the steppe of southern Russia. The Duel sets two decadent figures—a fanatical rationalist and a man of literary sensibility—on a collision course that ends in a series of surprising reversals. In The Story of an Unknown Man, a political radical spying on an important official by serving as valet to his son gradually discovers that his own terminal illness has changed his long-held priorities in startling ways. Three Years recounts a complex series of ironies in the personal life of a rich but passive Moscow merchant. In My Life, a man renounces wealth and social position for a life of manual labor.The resulting conflict between the moral simplicity of his ideals and the complex realities of human nature culminates       });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('bookCover_5697').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_5697').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_5697').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3565.Oscar_Wilde">About Oscar Wilde</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17913794017414907148">Oscar Fingal O'Flahertie Wills Wilde was an Irish playwright, poet, and author of numerous short stories, and one novel. Known for his biting wit, and a plentitude of aphorisms, he became one of the most successful playwrights of the late Victorian era in London, and one of the greatest celebrities of his day. Several of his plays continue to be widely performed, especially <i>The Importance of Being</i></span>
  <span id="freeText17913794017414907148" style="display:none">Oscar Fingal O'Flahertie Wills Wilde was an Irish playwright, poet, and author of numerous short stories, and one novel. Known for his biting wit, and a plentitude of aphorisms, he became one of the most successful playwrights of the late Victorian era in London, and one of the greatest celebrities of his day. Several of his plays continue to be widely performed, especially <i>The Importance of Being Earnest</i>. <br /><br />As the result of a widely covered series of trials, Wilde suffered a dramatic downfall and was imprisoned for two years hard labour after being convicted of "gross indecency" with other men. After Wilde was released from prison he set sail for Dieppe by the night ferry. He never returned to Ireland or Britain, and died in poverty.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17913794017414907148" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
